This Audit Report has been based on a selection of mortgage loans taken from the 6,925 mortgage 
loans, with a balance as at 25 October 2005 of Euros 526,108,073.63, that form the audited 
portfolio, using sampling techniques, which are a generally accepted method for verifying an 
entity's records relating to a group of items (“population”), and make it possible to draw a 
conclusion about that population through the analysis of a smaller number of items (“sample”) 
than the total population. The confidence level indicates the probability that the actual number of 
items with deviations from a pattern existing in a population will not exceed a predefined limit 
(“accuracy”).  
If the audit detects errors in any of the mortgage loans in the Sellers' portfolios, those loans will 
not be transferred on the Date of Incorporation. 
2.2.1. 
Legal jurisdiction by which the pool of assets is governed. 
The Participations and the Certificates relating to the Mortgage Loans will be issued in 
accordance with the laws of Spain. 
2.2.2. 
General characteristics of the Mortgagors. 
All the Mortgagors are private individuals. The details of the most significant 
characteristics of the selected mortgage loans are described throughout section 2. of this 
Additional Building Block. 
The tables below show the distribution of the mortgage loans that make up the audited 
portfolio by the geographical location of the security, contracted date, current balance, 
current rate, reference rate and spread, residual maturity, date of the next rate review and 
months in arrears. These tables have been produced with information as at 25 October 
2005.

2.2.3. 
Legal nature of the assets 
As indicated previously, all the assets will be Mortgage Loans that will be transferred to 
the Fund by the Sellers through the issue of Participations and Certificates. With respect 
to the audited portfolio, 86.18% of the outstanding nominal balance consists of mortgage 
participations and 13.82% of the outstanding nominal balance consists of mortgage 
transfer certificates, distributed among the Sellers as displayed below: 
 
Seller

The Mortgage Loans are divided into two categories, in line with their characteristics: 
-  
Mortgage Loans that meet the requirements of Section Two of the Ley del 
Mercado Hipotecario 2/1981, of 25 March (Mortgage Market Act - the “Ley 
del Mercado Hipotecario”) and that are transferred to the Fund through the 
issue of Participations (the “Mortgage Loans 1”). 
-  
Mortgage Loans that do not meet all the requirements of section two of the 
Ley del Mercado Hipotecario, including the requirements that mortgages 
must not exceed 80% of the appraised value of the mortgaged properties or 
that the mortgage loans must be secured by first-class real estate mortgages, 
which are transferred to the Fund through the issue of the Certificates, 
pursuant to article 18 of Ley 44/2002 (the “Mortgage Loans 2”). 
The Mortgage Loans are documented in public deeds and registered at the Land Registry, 
and can be foreclosed in accordance with the provisions of Title IV of Book III of the Ley 
de Enjuiciamiento 1/2000, of 7 January (Civil Procedural Act). 
2.2.4. 
Expiry or maturity date of the assets 
Each Mortgage Loan in the portfolio has a maturity date, without prejudice to the 
possibility of its early redemption, in accordance with the Special Terms and Conditions 
stipulated in each one.

At any time of the life of the Mortgage Loans, the Mortgagors can redeem all or part of 
the outstanding capital early, and interest will cease to accrue on the early redeemed part 
from the date on which the repayment is made. 
Section 2.2.2 of this Additional Building Block contains a chart with the distribution of 
the Mortgage Loans according to their residual maturity. The last regular redemption date 
of the mortgage loans is 10 June 2037. 
2.2.5. 
Amount of the assets 
On the Date of Incorporation, the Participations and Certificates that will be transferred to 
the Fund, with an Outstanding Nominal Balance equal to or slightly less than FOUR 
HUNDRED AND EIGHTY-FIVE million (485,000,000) euros, will be withdrawn from 
the loans in the portfolio audited as at 25 October 2005, which consists of 6,925 mortgage 
loans with an outstanding nominal balance of 526,108,073.63 euros.

2.2.7. 
Asset creation method 
CAJA CASTILLA LA MANCHA 
At the customer's request, the branch conducts a preliminary analysis and valuation with a 
view to the approval of the mortgage loan transaction. 
Normally during the first interview with customers, the following information is obtained 
about the transaction: information about the property, terms, financing needs, mortgages 
offered by other banks, etc. Customers are also told which type of loan best suits their 
needs, and about the nature, terms and conditions of the transaction (term, form of 
payment, expenses, rate of interest, etc.) and the documents that they must furnish. 
When the customers decide to apply for the loan and furnish all the documents and 
information requested, the branch office starts to process and analyse the application.  


This prospectus is a translation into English of the original "Folleto Informativo" drafted in Spanish language and registered with the 
"Comisión Nacional del Mercado de Valores" (the Spanish Securities Market Commission, "CNMV") on November 25h, 2005. The "Folleto 
Informativo" drafted in the Spanish language is the only official document, and no document other than the "Folleto Informativo"shall have 
any legal effect or be relied upon with regard to the Note Issue. 
 
82 
The branch processes the application in an automated fashion, requesting a property 
valuation, information from the CIRBE (Bank of Spain Central Risk Information 
Database) and the RAI Credit Bureau, and the other documentation necessary to assess 
the risk properly, according to internal regulations. 
When all the information has been obtained, a loan viability analysis is conducted that 
includes the use of a scoring programme. The main criterion underlying a decision to 
grant a loan is the customer's capacity to repay the loan on time, and any additional 
security or collateral is considered to support the transaction, but under no circumstances 
as a decision-making criterion. 
When all the information has been obtained, the branch office decides whether or not to 
grant the loan, if it is authorised to do so, or else submits the transaction for approval at a 
higher decision-making level authorised to do so. 
When the transaction has been authorised at the pertinent level, all the relevant documents 
are drawn up, the deed is signed in the presence of a Notary Public and all the legal 
formalities necessary for the transaction to be considered properly entered into are 
completed. 
Once a customer has furnished all the required documents, the transaction can be carried 
out within eight to ten days. 
In the case of subrogated loans, it is the property developer who gives CAJA CASTILLA 
LA MANCHA a list of the home buyers, as well as a copy of the private contracts of sale. 
The branch office handles the formalities with the customers, securing their prior 
commitment to be subrogated to the mortgage and requests the documents it needs to 
analyse the transaction. 
 
CREDIFIMO 
1.1.  Description of the process: 
Credifimo mainly engages in lending to private individuals, chiefly for home buying 
purposes and, to a lesser extent, consumer loans. 
Therefore most of its sales efforts are oriented to attracting customers interested in 
financing sales conducted through real estate agencies. Credifimo appoints area 
representatives who visit and advise a group of these agencies. Consequently the 
procedure for granting personal or mortgage loans is as follows: 
The real estate agent sends the area representative the application, together with proof of 
the applicant's level of income and the documents necessary for each type of transaction. 
If the area representative considers the application viable, after calculating the applicant's 
creditworthiness and job stability, refers the application to his/her Sales Manager. 
The Sales Manager analyses the viability of the transaction, asking the area representative 
and real estate agency for further documents (bank guarantees, additional documentation, 
additional real property as collateral, etc.) when deemed necessary. When all the 
information has been provided and if the Sales Manager considers the application viable, 
it is referred to the Risks Department, formed by a Risks Manager and six analysts with 
different types of duties, and the Deputy Director General makes the final decision. If the 
Risks Committee considers the loan viable after examining the report and the 
documentation, it issues a signed and dated report. If it is not viable, the application is 
rejected, or further collateral is requested and it is not processed.

payment of their social security contributions.

1.4. Delegation and autonomy criteria. 
Neither the Sales Managers, nor the regional offices or branch offices have decision-
making powers.  
1.5. Average duration of the process: 
Three days to make the decision and 20 days to process the application 
BANKPIME 
All asset transactions are originated through the branch offices, which attract customers 
either directly or through financial brokers. 
The following formalities are involved in granting an asset transaction: 
A) Processing and approval of transactions: 
•  
The transaction is simulated (using the parameters requested by the customer), the 
transaction form is completed and the signature/s of the applicant/s is/are obtained. 
•  
The branch checks that the transaction meets all the appropriate requirements, 
otherwise it will be rejected. 


This prospectus is a translation into English of the original "Folleto Informativo" drafted in Spanish language and registered with the 
"Comisión Nacional del Mercado de Valores" (the Spanish Securities Market Commission, "CNMV") on November 25h, 2005. The "Folleto 
Informativo" drafted in the Spanish language is the only official document, and no document other than the "Folleto Informativo"shall have 
any legal effect or be relied upon with regard to the Note Issue. 
 
84 
• 
The customer is asked to furnish all the required documentation.  
•  
The customer is given a leaflet and a copy of the simulation. 
•  
The application and the documents furnished are examined. 
•  
Queries are made to the RAI, Asnef and CIRBE (Bank of Spain Central Risk 
Information Database). 
•  
The bank requests a property register search and a valuation of the property. 
•  
The transaction is analysed to find out more about the transaction and orient the 
proposal. Any transactions that pose problems are rejected. 
•  
The transaction is submitted to the competent body, which makes the final 
decision and the result is reported to the branch office 
•  
Approved applications are sent to the processing department. 
B)  Processing of transactions 
•  
In this phase, the transaction is processed in the computer system and the documents 
are prepared for signing. 
•  
The processing department receives the dossier from the Analysis Department, and 
checks that the decision sheet has been signed by the people authorised to do so. 
•  
The asset transaction is processed in the computer system and signed before a 
Notary Public. 
•  
The processing officer informs the branch office of the cost of any cancellation 
charges that have to be paid. 
•  
In transactions subject to special terms and conditions on account of the applicant's 
customer status, the processing centre emails the branch office an annex to the 
contract, stating that the lower than standard terms and conditions will remain in 
force provided certain status-related requirements are met. 
•  
The transaction must be accompanied by a fire insurance policy for the property and 
life assurance policy for the applicants, if this has not been issued by the branch 
office. The processing officer completes the appropriate online insurance policy 
application form with the details of the policyholder and the insured party. If the 
customer has already taken out the required insurance policies, he/she must ask the 
insurance companies to include a new clause in favour of BANKPIME and send 
them to the processing centre, which will file them in the dossier. 
•  
The branch office is responsible for arranging the signing of the loan with the 
customer, in the presence of the notary public. 
•  
A different processing officer checks that all the electronic files have been 
completed correctly by comparing them with the information in the mortgage deed. 
•  
After confirming that the information is correct, the officer completes the loan 
arrangement formalities, charging the valuation, land registry search and 
downpayment to the customer's account, and transfers the downpayment to the 
administrative agency (which is informed by e-mail). 
•  
The processing department is responsible for supervising the administrative agency's 
work, tax payments and registration of the mortgage in the land register. When these

the centralized archive and the copies of the mortgage loan in a fireproof cabinet. 
•  
Processing officers have a checklist that lists all the steps and tasks involved in 
arranging a mortgage loan, and tick off each one as and when it is completed, 
thereby ensuring that all the tasks are done, especially when more than one person is 
involved in arranging a loan. 
A mortgage loan proposal must contain the following documents: 
•  
Asset transaction application form signed by the applicants 
•  
Simulation of the transaction (with the parameters requested by the customer) 
•  
Proposing party's report 
•  
Private contract of sale, and deposit contract. 
•  
Photocopies of the owners' National Identity Cards, passport or residence permit

Copy of the insurance policy or application for insurance policy for the property to 
be mortgaged 
•  
Copy of the owner's life insurance policy or life insurance application 
•  
Previous year's Personal Income Tax return and Wealth Tax return (where 
applicable) 
•  
Documentation of the property to be mortgaged 
BANKPIME has decided to implement a centralized model to handle all of the Bank's 
credit risk, through a single “RISKS DEPARTMENT” 
All decisions regarding credit risk transactions will be made by a single Risk Committee. 
The duties of the Risk Committee are as follows: 
•  
To analyse and make decisions regarding the terms, conditions and collateral of 
credit risk transactions 
•  
To submit and explain the transactions to the Executive Committee for approval 
and, where applicable, to discuss the transactions with the assistance of the 
Technical Secretariat. 
•  
To submit proposals regarding its powers to the Executive Committee. 
The frequency of the Risk Committee meetings depends on the number of transactions, 
but it meets at least once a week. 
Any transactions that, alone or together with the rest of a corporate group's risks, exceed 
€300,000, must be approved by the Executive Committee. 
The Risks Committee is the only body authorised to grant risks. 
On average, it takes between 7 and 12 days to grant a mortgage loan.

2.2.8.2 
With regard to the Participations and the Certificates 
The Participations and the Certificates will meet the following characteristics on the 
Date of Incorporation. 
(1) 
That the Participations and the Certificates are being issued pursuant to the 
Ley del Mercado Hipotecario, Royal Decree 685/1982 and the Fifth 
Additional Provision of the Ley 3/1994, as reworded in article 18 of the Ley 
44/2002 and other applicable regulations and comply with all the 
requirements established therein for the issue of mortgage participations; and, 
in particular, that the issue of the Mortgage Participations conforms to the 
provisions of articles 59 and 62 of Royal Decree 685/1982, regarding the 
volume of mortgage-backed obligations issued by the Seller. The mortgage 
participations are being issued with the backing of the Mortgage Loans 1, 
which comply with all the requirements set forth in Section II of the Ley del 
Mercado Hipotecario and in Chapter II of Royal Decree 685/1982, and the 
Mortgage Transfer Certificates are being issued with the backing of the 
Mortgage Loans 2, which do not comply with all the requirements set forth in 
Section II of the Ley del Mercado Hipotecario and in Chapter II of Royal 
Decree 685/1982, all pursuant to the provisions of the Fifth Additional 
Provision of the Ley 3/1994, as reworded in article 18 of the Ley 44/2002. 
(2) 
That the respective corporate bodies of the Sellers have validly adopted all 
the agreements necessary for the issue of the Participations and the 
Certificates.

The Mortgage Loans will meet the following characteristics on the Date of Incorporation. 
(1) 
That the Mortgage Loans exist, are valid and enforceable in accordance with 
current legislation, and that all of the applicable legal provisions have been 
respected in the granting thereof. 
(2) 
That it is the fee simple owner of all the Mortgage Loans, and there is no 
impediment to it issuing the Participations and the Certificates that represent 
Mortgage Loans. 
(3) 
That the information given about the Mortgage Loans in Appendix 4 to the 
Articles of Incorporation and the information included on the Multiple 
Certificates, will correctly reflect their status on the Date of Incorporation, as is 
described in the computer files sent about the loans, and that such information is 
correct, complete and not misleading. Any other additional information about the 
nature of the Seller's mortgage loan portfolio given in this Prospectus is correct 
and not misleading. 
(4) 
That all the Mortgage Loans accrue interest at variable rates, even though fixed 
rates may have been agreed during the initial period, and that applicable interest 
rate caps and/or floors may have been established. 
(5) 
That the Mortgage Loans have been granted to natural persons for the purposes 
of the purchase, construction or rehabilitation of properties located in Spain. 
Some of the said loans have been subrogated to private individuals from 
financing granted to developers for housing built for sale. 
(6) 
That all the Mortgage Loans backing the issue of Mortgage Participations 
secured by a first-class real estate mortgage. 
(7) 
 That all the Mortgage Loans backing the issue of Mortgage Transfer Certificates 
can be secured by second-class mortgages, provided that, in this case, (i) the 
mortgagee is the same Seller for the first and second mortgage, (ii) the sum of 
the nominal balances does not exceed 100% of the appraised value for the 
Mortgage Loans and, (iii) the Seller undertakes to handle the first mortgage in a 
manner that does not have a negative effect on the second mortgage.  
(8) 
That all the mortgages has been properly raised and registered in the pertinent 
Land Registries and the registration details match the details given in the Articles 
of Incorporation of the Fund and in the corresponding Multiple Certificates. The 
registration of the mortgaged properties is valid and free of any contradiction and 
is not subject to any preferential limitation upon the mortgage in accordance with 
applicable regulations. 
(9) 
That the mortgages have been raised on properties of which the mortgagors are 
the full fee simple owners, that they meet the requirements set forth in article 27 
of Royal Decree 685/1982 and the Seller has no knowledge of any disputes 
relating to the ownership of such properties, without the mortgage properties 
being subject to any disposal prohibitions, conditions subsequent or any other 
ownership limitation. 
(10) 
that all the mortgaged properties are completed properties and have been 
appraised by Valuation Companies registered with the Bank of Spain, evidence 
of the valuation being furnished in the form of the pertinent certificate. The 
valuations comply with all the requirements established in the laws governing

2.2.9. 
Substitution of the securitised assets 
In the exceptional event that, after the Date of Incorporation and, notwithstanding the 
declarations made by each Seller and the diligence exercised by the latter in ensuring their 
truthfulness, it is found, during life of the Fund, that one of the Participations and/or 
Certificates or that one of the Mortgage Loans upon which the latter have been issued, did 
not conform, on the Date of Incorporation of the Fund, to the declarations made in section 
2.2.8. of this Additional Building Block and set forth in Clause 8.3. of the Articles of 
Incorporation, the Sellers undertake as follows: 
(A) To substitute the Participation and/or Certificate in question with another of similar 
financial characteristics, in terms of the amount, residual term, interest rate, 
characteristics 
of 
the 
mortgagor 
and 
mortgaged 
property 
and 
current 
balance/appraised value ratio, that is accepted by the Sociedad Gestora, reported to 
the Rating Agencies and provided that it does not affect the Securities ratings 
granted by such Agencies. 
The amounts accrued and unpaid until the date of substitution of the Participation 
and/or Certificate that is to be substituted, must be paid to the Fund by the Seller in 
question, in its capacity as administrator, at the time that such Participation and/or 
Certificate is substituted. 
Be that as it may, when substituting a Participation and/or Certificate, the Sellers 
must attest that the substitute Participation and/or Certificate conforms to the 
declarations set forth in section 2.2.8. of this Additional Building Block. 
As soon as each Seller learns that one of the Participations and/or Certificates that it 
has issued or that one of the Mortgage Loans underlying them does not conform the 
aforementioned declarations, it will report the matter to the Sociedad Gestora and, 
within five (5) days, indicate the mortgage loans with respect to which it intends to

issue new mortgage participations and/or mortgage transfer certificates to substitute 
the ones affected. If any Participation and/or Certificate is substituted, pursuant to 
the provisions of this paragraph, the Seller in question will proceed to issue a new 
Multiple Certificate that will be exchanged for the certificate that was issued on the 
Date of Incorporation. 
The Seller in question undertakes to formalize the substitution of Participations and 
Certificates in a public deed and in the manner and time frame stipulated by the 
Sociedad Gestora, and to furnish any related information that the Sociedad Gestora 
deems necessary. The substitution will be reported to the Rating Agencies and a 
copy of the deed will be sent to the CNMV. 
(B) In addition to the obligation assumed in point (A) supra and whenever the 
substitution stipulated therein is not possible because the mortgage loans available 
are not homogeneous with the securitised portfolio in terms of (i) the amount, (ii) 
the residual term, (iii) the interest rate, (iv) the characteristics of the mortgagor, (v) 
the characteristics of the mortgaged property, or (vi) current balance/appraised value 
ratio, the Seller in question undertakes to proceed to the early redemption of the 
Participation and/or Certificate in question, by reimbursing, in cash, both the 
outstanding capital of the Participation and/or Certificate in question and the interest 
accrued and unpaid to date, as well as payable any other amount owing to the Fund 
with respect to the Participation and/or Certificate in question, by depositing it in the 
Collection Account. The amounts received from the Participations and/or 
Certificates in question in the aforementioned circumstances will be added to the 
Available Funds and applied on the next Payment Date. 
In particular, should the Seller in question modify the terms and conditions of the 
Mortgage Loans during their lifetime without complying with the limits established in the 
special legislation applicable and with the terms agreed between the Fund and the Seller 
in the Articles of Incorporation of the Fund and in this Prospectus, in section 3.7.1. of this 
Additional Building Block, the Seller will be considered in breach of its obligations and 
the Fund will not be held responsible. In the event of such breach, the Fund, through the 
Sociedad Gestora, will be entitled to (i) seek pertinent damages and (ii) seek the 
substitution or reimbursement of the Participations and/or Certificates in question, 
pursuant to the provisions of letters (A) and (B) supra. This will not imply that the Seller 
guarantees the success of the transaction, but the necessary redress of the effects caused 
by the breach of its obligations, pursuant to article 1,124 of the Civil Code. The expenses 
originating from the actions to remedy the breach of the Seller will be borne by the latter 
and may not be recovered from the Fund. 
The Sociedad Gestora will notify the CNMV immediately whenever Loans are substituted 
or redeemed as a result of breach by the Sellers. 
2.2.10. Relevant insurance policies relating to the securitised assets 
Pursuant to the declarations and warranties set forth in section 2.2.8. of the Additional 
Building Block, all the properties mortgaged as security for the Mortgage Loans are 
insured against damages by insurance policies in favour of the Seller in question, in which 
the insured sum is not less than the valuation of the mortgaged property, excluding items 
which by their nature are uninsurable. For these purposes, Caja Castilla La Mancha and 
Bankpime has taken out a global subsidiary insurance policy that guarantees damage 
insurance coverage if none exists or if the insured sums are insufficient..

3.3.1. 
General Terms for the issuance and subscription of the Participations and the

outstanding principal of each of the Mortgage Loans, and accruing interest at a rate equal 
to the nominal interest rate accrued by each corresponding Mortgage Loan. The amount

The full and unconditional assignment to the Fund of the credit rights which are derived 
from the Mortgage Loans, with the exceptions noted in section 3.3.3 of this Additional 
Building Block, by means of the issuance of the Participations and Certificates, will take 
place on the Date of Incorporation for the remaining term to maturity of said Loans, with 
no agreement of any kind to repurchase on the part of the Sellers. The Participations and 
the Certificates will begin to accrue the corresponding interest, beginning on the Date of 
Incorporation (inclusive), which is 28 November 2005, with the result that the interest 
accrued on the Mortgage Loans beginning on the Date of Incorporation will be for the 
benefit of the Fund, irrespective of the actual accrual period used to calculate the interest 
payment on said loans. 
The Sellers will not assume any responsibility whatsoever for non-payment by the 
Mortgagors, whether for principal, interest, or any other amount which the Mortgagors 
may owe pursuant to the Mortgage Loans. Likewise, they will not be held liable, in any 
form whatsoever, for directly or indirectly guaranteeing the successful conclusion of this 
transaction, nor will they grant collateral or bank guarantees, nor will they enter into 
agreements to repurchase the Participations and the Certificates, whether pursuant to the 
Articles of Incorporation, or to this Prospectus, or to any other agreement or contract. 
Each Seller will warrant to the Fund the existence and validity of the Mortgage Loans in 
the same manner as specified by articles 348 of the Commercial Code and 1,529 of the 
Civil Code. 
3.3.2. 
Issuance Price of the Participations and the Certificates 
The Sociedad Gestora, on the Date of Incorporation, will subscribe to 100% of the 
Participations and the Certificates on behalf of the Fund. 
The price of the Participations and the Certificates will be the Outstanding Nominal 
Balance thereof as of the Date of Incorporation and will be paid by the Sociedad Gestora, 
on behalf of and for the account of the Fund, to each Seller, on the Disbursement Date, 
which is 1 December 2005. 
In the event of termination of the incorporation of the Fund and, consequently, of the 
issuance and subscription of the Participations and of the Certificates, (i) the obligation of 
the Fund to pay for the Participations and the Certificates will be extinguished, and (ii) 
the Sociedad Gestora will be obligated to restore to the Sellers any right which may have 
accrued to the Fund by the subscription of the respective Participations and Certificates. 
In this event of the early termination of the Fund, the Sellers will undertake to meet any 
initial expenses that may have been incurred in incorporating the Fund, each one paying a 
percentage equivalent to its percentage participation in the issue of Mortgage 
Participations and Mortgage Transfer Certificates and taking into account any expenses 
that can attributed individually to each one of them.  
3.3.3. 
Description of the rights conferred upon the Fund for the subscription of the 
Mortgage Loan Participations and Certificates 
The Fund, as legal holder of the Participations and the Certificates, will hold the rights 
generally recognized by applicable law and in the Participations and the Certificates. 
Specifically, the Fund will be entitled to receive the payments which, beginning on the 
Date of Incorporation, are made by the Mortgagors, with the exceptions noted in the 
following paragraph, as well as any other payments arising from the Mortgage Loans, 
whenever they are made in accordance with the Participations and Certificates.  


This prospectus is a translation into English of the original "Folleto Informativo" drafted in Spanish language and registered with the 
"Comisión Nacional del Mercado de Valores" (the Spanish Securities Market Commission, "CNMV") on November 25h, 2005. The "Folleto 
Informativo" drafted in the Spanish language is the only official document, and no document other than the "Folleto Informativo"shall have

In addition to the payments made by the Mortgagors, the Fund will be entitled to any 
other payment received by the Sellers on the Mortgage Loans, as administrators of these 
loans, including those arising from any right related to the loan such as those payments 
arising from insurance policies, payments made by possible guarantors, etc. with the 
exception of default interest, fees for the collection of unpaid amounts, assumption fees, 
early redemption/cancellation fees, as well as any other fee or payment to which the 
Sellers of the Participations and the Certificates are entitled.  
In addition, the Fund will be entitled to receive amounts, goods, or rights as payment of 
principal or interest on the Mortgage Loans, whether based on liquidation price or an 
amount determined by a court order or notarial procedure in the enforcement of a 
mortgage guarantee, by the transfer or liquidation of the real estate awarded or as a 
consequence of the aforementioned enforcement actions, as the acting administrator and 
manager of the properties in the process of foreclosure. The Sellers agree to provide the 
appropriate notifications that, depending on the case, are needed in order for said 
payments to be made to the Sociedad Gestora.  
The Sellers will exercise reasonable effort in order to maintain in full force and effect the 
insurance policies purchased relative to the Mortgage Loans, with each Seller being liable 
to the Fund for any loss sustained by the Fund in the event that the insurance policies are 
not maintained in full force and effect. 
 
3.3.4. 
Representation of the Participations and the Certificates and the deposit thereof 
The Participations and the Certificates that are pooled in the Fund will be represented by 
six (6) Multiple Certificates, three (3) Multiple Certificates issued, respectively, by CAJA 
CASTILLA LA MANCHA, CREDIFIMO and BANKPIME, representing all the 
Participations issued by each one of them, and three (3) Multiple Certificates issued, 
respectively, by CAJA CASTILLA LA MANCHA, CREDIFIMO and BANKPIME 
representing all the Certificates issued by each one of them. 
Both in the event that the Sociedad Gestora proceeds, on behalf and for the account of the 
Fund, to substitute a Mortgage Loan in accordance with the provisions of section 2.2.9 
(40).of the Additional Building Block, and in the event that a Mortgage Loan is 
foreclosed, in accordance with the provisions of section 3.7.1. of this Additional Building 
Block, and if, in the event of the Early Liquidation of the Fund, on the grounds and 
according to the terms set forth in section 4.4.3. of the Registration Document, the 
Participations and/or the Certificates have to be sold, and for any other circumstances 
which may arise, the Sellers undertake to divide any Multiple Certificate representing the 
Participations and/or the Certificates into as many individual or multiples certificates as 
may be required, or to substitute or exchange them, in order to achieve the 
aforementioned purposes. 
The Multiple Certificates representing the Participations and the Certificates and, in a 
given case, the individual certificates into which they have been divided, will remain on 
deposit with the Payment Agent who will act as the depository for them.

transferable by written declaration on the security itself and, generally, by any of the

3.3.6. 
Notification of the Mortgagors 
The Sellers will continue servicing the Mortgage Loans, in accordance with the 
provisions of section 3.7.1. of this Securities Note. The Sociedad Gestora and the Sellers 
will agree not to notify their respective Mortgagors of the transfer on the Date of 
Incorporation of the Fund. 
 
Notwithstanding the foregoing, the Sociedad Gestora will instruct the Sellers as to their 
obligation to notify the Mortgagors of the transfer of the Mortgage Loans, as and when it 
deems it appropriate, and in any case, in the event that the Sellers are substituted as the 
servicers of the Mortgage Loans, as well as in the event of the insolvency of the Sellers. 
The transfer must be notified by the reliable means of communications that the Sociedad 
Gestora considers fastest and most effective. 
3.4. 
Explanation of the flow of funds 
3.4.1. 
How the cash flow from the assets will meet the issuer’s obligations to the Security 
holders 
As illustrated in the diagram included in section 3.1. of this Additional Building Block, 
the cash flow from the assets will serve to fulfil the obligations of the issuer in the 
following manner: 
a) On the Disbursement Date, the Fund will pay the price of the Participations and of 
the Certificates issued, with a portion of the principal amount received from the 
Bonds. 
b) On said Disbursement Date, the Fund will also receive the amount of the Initial 
Expenses Loan, provided that the drawdown condition set forth in section 3.4.3.2. 
of the Additional Building Block is met. 
c) Likewise, on said Disbursement Date, the Reserve Fund will be established from a 
portion of the issuance price of the Securities. 
d) On each Collection Date corresponding to each Seller, the Sociedad Gestora, for 
and on behalf of the Fund, will receive the amounts that the Fund should receive 
respectively from each of the Sellers that have been paid by their Mortgagors for 
principal and interest during the Calculation Period. These amounts will remain on 
deposit in the Collection Account, earning interest, in accordance with the 
provisions of the Financial Services Contract, and will be utilized to meet the Fund 
payment requirements on each Payment Date. 
e) Technical Advance. Taking into account that a portion of the delays in the 
payment of an instalment by the Mortgagors can be of a temporary or technical 
nature, in order to prevent any such delays from negatively affecting the flow of

Informativo" drafted in the Spanish language is the only official document, and no document other than the "Folleto Informativo"shall have 
any legal effect or be relied upon with regard to the Note Issue.

payments to the holders of the Securities issued, and in addition taking into 
account the existence of a 20 day difference between the end of the Calculation 
Period and the Calculation Date by the Fund during which period of time the 
amounts are collected by each Seller, as administrator of its respective Mortgage 
Loans, which belong to the Fund, the Sociedad Gestora will on each Calculation 
Date be entitled to draw, acting on behalf of and for the account of the Fund, a 
payment advance to be charged against said amounts.  
The amount of each Technical Advance will be an amount not greater than the 
amount collected by each Seller, from the Loans which it services, for any 
payments to which the Fund is entitled as holder of the Participations and the 
Certificates, from the end of the most recent Calculation Period until the 
Calculation Date on which the Technical Advance is requested. 
On each Calculation Date, the Technical Advance obtained on the previous 
Calculation Date will be considered deductible in the Calculation Period that is to 
be paid, and another Technical Advance may be requested from the next Technical 
Advance and charged to the next payment. 
f) The amounts received from the Mortgage Loans corresponding to the three (3) 
Collection Periods prior to the corresponding Payment Date, the amount of the 
Technical Advance, the interest accrued on the Collection Account, on the 
Treasury Account, on the Liquidity Line Sinking Account, and if applicable, on 
the Reinvestment Accounts and on the Treasury Surplus Account, the Net Amount 
which results in favour of the Fund pertaining to the Derivative Contracts and the 
amount which at any given moment comprises the Reserve Fund will be utilized 
on each Payment Date, to pay the accrued interest and repay principal on the 
Securities in accordance with the Payment Priority Order described in section 
3.4.6. of the Additional Building Block.  
3.4.2. 
Information on any credit enhancements 
As a mechanism for credit enhancement in the event of possible losses from unpaid 
and/or defaulted Mortgage Loans and for the purpose of allowing payments to be made 
by the Fund in accordance with the Payment Priority Order, a provision for the 
establishment of the Reserve Fund has been made, initially funded with a portion of the 
issuance price of the Securities. 
Similarly, the postponement in the payment of interest and the return of principal between 
the different Classes which results from their ranking in the Payment Priority Order, as 
well as the redemption rules for each of the Series established in section 4.9.2. of the 
Securities Note, constitute a protection mechanism between the different Classes. 
In order to eliminate the interest rate risk which exists due to the fact that the 
Participations and the Certificates are subject to variable interest rates based on different 
index rates and different adjustment periods and payment periods for the variable interest 
payments established for each of the Classes that are issued and paid by the Fund, the 
Sociedad Gestora will enter into three Derivative Contracts, described in section 3.4.7.1. 
of this Additional Building Block, with BSBP. 
In general, the quality of the Mortgage Loans and of the financial safeguards and controls, 
established in order to maintain the financial stability of the Fund, are such that they are 
considered sufficient by the Rating Agencies in order to assign the provisional solvency 
ratings to each one of the Securities that are included in section 7.5. of the Securities 
Note.

Details of any financing  
3.4.3.1 
Liquidity Line Contract 
The Sellers will grant, in accordance with the provisions of the Liquidity Line Contract, a 
liquidity line to the Fund (the “Liquidity Line”) for a total maximum amount of one 
million nine hundred and forty thousand (1,940,000) euros, equivalent to 0.4% of the 
original balance of the Bond issue, distributed among them in the following manner:  
 
 
CAJA CASTILLA LA MANCHA: 1,240,048 euros. 
 
 
CREDIFIMO: 
 
             519,920 euros. 
 
 
BANKPIME:                         
 180,032 euros. 
The maximum amount of the Liquidity Line will be made available on the Disbursement 
Date, and will be deposited in the Liquidity Line Sinking Account. 
On the first Payment Date, if necessary, the Sociedad Gestora will order a transfer from 
Liquidity Line Sinking Account to cover the shortfall that exists on that date between the 
interest accrued of the Participations and Certificates until that Payment Date and the 
interest collected on the Participations and Certificates, during the Calculation Periods 
prior to the first Payment Date. 
Where applicable, the remaining amounts not used to cover the shortfall indicated in the 
previous paragraph of this section and deposited in the Liquidity Line Sinking Account 
will also be transferred on the first Payment Date to the Treasury Account and will be 
used to repay part of the Liquidity Line on that date according to the Payment Priority 
Order.  
If, on the first Payment Date, the shortfall described above does not exist, the whole 
amount deposited in the Liquidity Line Sinking Account must be transferred to the 
Treasury Account on the first Payment Date, and such amount will be used to repay the 
whole of the Liquidity Line on that date according to the Payment Priority Order. 
The amounts drawn under the Liquidity Line and subject to repayment will accrue an 
interest rate equal to the rate that results from reducing the monthly average of the 
EONIA rates, calculated in accordance with the provisions of the Liquidity Line Contract, 
by fifteen (15) basis points, if the Liquidity Line has not been repaid in full on the first 
Payment Date. Such interest will be settled quarterly on each Payment Date and will be 
subject to the Payment Priority Order set forth in section 3.4.6. of the Additional Building 
Block.  
On each Payment Date, in accordance with the Payment Priority Order, an allocation will 
be made for the repayment of the Liquidity Line which will be accumulated in the 
Liquidity Line Sinking Fund deposited in the Liquidity Line Sinking Account, in the 
amount necessary so that, on each Payment Date, the balance of said Account will be 
equal to the amount resulting by applying to the amount available under the Liquidity 
Line and not repaid on the First Payment Date the percentage by which the Outstanding 
Nominal Balance under the Participations and Certificates has been reduced on the last 
day of the Calculation Period immediately prior to the corresponding Payment Date, 
relative to the Outstanding Nominal Balance on the Date of Incorporation. 
On the Payment Date on which the Outstanding Nominal Balance under the Participations 
and Certificates falls below 10% of the initial amount of the same:

Initial Expenses Loan Contract 
The Sellers will grant, in accordance with the provisions of the Initial Expenses Loan 
Contract, a loan to the Fund (the “Initial Expenses Loan”), for the purpose of meeting the 
initial expenses of the Fund, for a maximum amount equal to 1,079,505 Euros, which will

In the event that, once the definitive amount of the NAS-IO securities has been 
established, it is found that the proceeds from the Securities issued will be enough to 
cover both the price of the Mortgage Loans, the allocation of the Reserve Fund (as 
established in section 3.4.3.3.) and the payment of the initial expenses of the Fund, the 
Initial Expenses Loan will not be made available and the Initial Expenses Loan Contract 
will be terminated. Be that as it may, the termination of the Initial Expenses Contract on 
these grounds will not imply any additional expense for the Fund. 
Therefore the definitive amount of the Initial Expenses Loan or, where applicable, the 
termination of such Loan, will be determined by the Sociedad Gestora on 29 November 
2005, once the definitive amount of the NAS-IO Securities has been determined as 
described in section 4.2. of the Securities Note. The Sociedad Gestora will proceed to 
notify the final amount of the Initial Expenses Loan or, where applicable, the termination 
of the Contract, before 14:00 (CET time) on 29 November 2005, before the start of the 
Subscription Period. The final amount of the Initial Expenses Loan will be delivered, 
where applicable, on the Disbursement Date by means of a deposit into the Treasury 
Account. The final amount of the Initial Expenses Loan or, where applicable, the 
termination of such Loan, will be documented in the notarized disbursement document. 
The amount of the Initial Expenses Loan will be used by the Sociedad Gestora for the 
purpose of paying the initial expenses of the Fund incurred  in the incorporation of the 
Fund and the issuance of the Securities. 
If the Initial Expenses Loan is used, the interest on it will be calculated based on an 
annual interest rate, adjusted quarterly, equal to the Reference Interest Rate of the 
Securities in force from time to time. This interest will be paid only if the Fund has 
sufficient liquidity available according to the Payment Priority Order. The interest will be 
settled on each Payment Date, and will be calculated on the following basis: (i) the actual 
effective days in each Interest Accrual Period and (ii) a 360 day year 
The Loan principal will be repaid in 20 equal and consecutive instalments, the first of 
which will be paid on the first Payment Date (March 22, 2006) and the remaining ones on 
the following Payment Dates, all being subject to the Payment Priority Order described in 
section 3.4.6. of the Additional Building Block. 
The non-confirmation before the start of the Subscription Period of one of the provisional 
ratings assigned to the Securities by the Rating Agencies will be construed as grounds for

3.4.3.3 
Reserve Fund 
As a security measure and for the purpose of allowing payments to be made by the Fund 
according to the Payment Priority Order described in section 3.4.6. of the Additional 
Building Block, a reserve fund will be established entitled “Reserve Fund”. 
The Reserve Fund will be initially established on the Disbursement Date, funded by a 
portion of the issuance price of the Securities, after having paid in full the price of the 
Participations and the Certificates, in the amount of THREE MILLION NINE 
HUNDRED AND SEVENTY SEVEN THOUSAND (3,977,000) euros. 
On each Payment Date, the resources available on each Payment Date for that purpose, 
according to the Payment Priority Order, will be allocated to the Reserve Fund until the 
required level is reached for that Payment Date (hereafter referred to as the “Required 
Level”). 
The Required Level will be the lesser of the following amounts: 
- 0.82% of the initial amount of the Bond issuance. 
- 1.64% of the Outstanding Nominal Balance of the Bond issuance.  
The Reserve Fund must not be reduced in the event that any of the following 
circumstances exists: 
1) 
That the Reserve Fund is not at its Required Level as of the prior Payment 
Date. 
2) 
That the Outstanding Nominal Balance of the Participations and the 
Certificates that are past due for 90 days or more exceeds 1% of the 
Outstanding Nominal Balance of the Participations and the Certificates. 
3) 
That 3 years have not elapsed since the Date of Incorporation. 
In any event, the Required Level of the Reserve Fund must not fall below 0.5% of the 
initial balance of the Bond issuance. 
The amounts which make up the Reserve Fund will be deposited in the Treasury Account 
under the terms referred to in section 3.4.4.2. of the Additional Building Block.

3.4.4. 
Parameters for the investment of temporary liquidity surpluses and a description of 
the parties responsible for such investment 
The investment parameters for the liquidity surpluses of the Fund are listed in the 
Financial Services Contract. 
3.4.4.1 
Collection Account  
The Fund will have available through the Payment Agent, in accordance with the 
provisions of the Financial Services Contract, a bank account on behalf of the Fund (the 
“Collection Account”), through which it will accept on each Collection Date, from each 
Seller, in accordance with the dates stipulated in section 4.9.2.2. of the Securities Note, all 
of the payments that the Fund should receive from each of the Sellers respectively 
resulting from the loans which it services. 
CAJA CASTILLA LA MANCHA and CREDIFIMO will make their payments on a 
weekly basis, each Tuesday or, if is not a Business Day, on the immediately next 
Business Day. BANKPIME will make its payments on the 4th and 19th of each month or, 
if either of these is not a Business Day, the immediately next Business Day.  
Nevertheless, should the short-term debt rating assigned to the Sellers by either of the 
Rating Agencies have a negative effect on the Bond rating assigned by such Rating 
Agency, the Sellers will make their deposits on a daily basis. 
Additionally, in the event that the rating of CAJA DE AHORROS PROVINCIAL DE 
SAN FERNANDO DE SEVILLA Y JEREZ, in its capacity as the parent company of 
CREDIFIMO, assigned by any of the Rating Agencies to its subordinated and unsecured 
debt, is downgraded below F2, on the Fitch short-term rating scale and/or below A-, on 
the Fitch long-term rating scale, or else the aforementioned entity ceases to own 51% of 
the shares into which the share capital of CREDIFIMO are divided, and in such an event 
another entity with the same or higher ratings as CAJA DE AHORROS PROVINCIAL 
DE SAN FERNANDO DE SEVILLA Y JEREZ on the long-term and short-term rating 
scales of Fitch does not gain control of  51% of the shares into which the share capital of 
CREDIFIMO is divided, the latter must make its deposits on a daily basis. 
Additionally, in the event that the rating assigned by Fitch to the non-subordinated and 
unsecured debt of CAJA CASTILLA LA MANCHA is downgraded to a rating equal to 
F2, on the Fitch short-term rating scale, CAJA CASTILLA LA MANCHA will make its 
deposits on alternate days, instead of every week. If the rating assigned to that entity 
downgraded below F1, according to the Fitch scale, CAJA CASTILLA LA MANCHA 
will make its deposits on a daily basis and, additionally, must obtain a guarantee similar 
to the one described in section 3.4.4.3. (iii) of this Additional Building Block. 
The amounts that have been deposited in the Collection Account and that represent the 
total collected amount, derived from the mortgage loans serviced by each of the Sellers 
during the calendar month prior to each Calculation Date (hereafter referred to as 
“Collected Amount”) will be deposited, along with the corresponding Technical 
Advance, into the Treasury Account before 11:30 (CET time) on the corresponding 
Calculation Date, with good value as of that same date.  
The earnings on the Collection Account will be transferred on each Payment Date to the 
Treasury Account. 
The Collection Account will not be allowed to have a negative balance to the detriment of 
the Fund. 


This prospectus is a translation into English of the original "Folleto Informativo" drafted in Spanish language and registered with the 
"Comisión Nacional del Mercado de Valores" (the Spanish Securities Market Commission, "CNMV") on November 25h, 2005. The "Folleto 
Informativo" drafted in the Spanish language is the only official document, and no document other than the "Folleto Informativo"shall have 
any legal effect or be relied upon with regard to the Note Issue.

The amounts deposited into the Collection Account will accrue interest on behalf of the 
Fund, with said interest to be paid monthly (on the last day of each month), calculated 
based on an annual interest rate equal to the rate that results from reducing the reference 
rate, which will be the monthly average of the EONIA rates, calculated in accordance 
with the provisions of the Financial Services Contract, by fifteen (15) basis points. Said 
amount will be rounded up to the nearest hundredth.  
In the event that the short-term risk rating of the Payment Agent assigned by any of the 
Rating Agencies, which is currently listed as F1+ by Fitch and A-1 by S&P, were 
downgraded to a rating lower than F1 according to the Fitch rating system and/or lower 
than A-1 according to S&P, or if that rating were to be discontinued, for whatever reason, 
by any of the Rating Agencies, the Sociedad Gestora must initiate, on behalf of the Fund, 
the options described in section 5.2 of the Securities Note. 
In the event that, at any given moment, the balance in the Collection Account, together 
with the balance of the Treasury Account and the balance of the Liquidity Line Sinking 
Account, were to be greater than or equal to 20% of the Outstanding Nominal Amount of 
the Bonds, the Sociedad Gestora will move such excess, until the following Payment 
Date, at which time it will be returned to the appropriate account to be applied, into an 
account with an entity whose short term unsubordinated and unsecured debt is rated A-1+ 
by S&P and F1 by Fitch, seeking to obtain the highest earnings possible on these 
balances. (Hereafter, the account which is opened, in accordance with the provisions 
immediately preceding in this paragraph, will be referred to as the “Treasury Surplus 
Account”). 
In the event that the short term debt rating for this entity in which the Treasury Surplus 
Account is opened is downgraded below A-1+, according to the S&P rating system and 
F1, according to the Fitch rating system, the Sociedad Gestora will have a period of thirty 
(30) days to find a substitute entity whose short term unsubordinated and unsecured debt 
is rated A-1+ by S&P and F1 by Fitch, or a guarantee payable on demand from an entity 
whose short term debt is rated A-1+ by S&P and F1 by Fitch. 
3.4.4.2 
Treasury Account 
The Fund will have available through the Payment Agent, in accordance with the 
provisions in the Financial Services Contract, a bank account on behalf of the Fund 
(hereafter referred to as “Treasury Account”).  
On each Calculation Date, the Fund will transfer to the Treasury Account all of the 
receipts which the Fund should receive of the Sellers from the Collection Account, in 
accordance with the provisions of the previous section and of the Articles of 
Incorporation. 
The allocation for the Reserve Fund and the Net Amounts in favour of the Fund from the 
Derivative Contracts will also be placed into the Treasury Account.  
Likewise, on the Disbursement Date, each Seller will deposit, where applicable, the actual 
amount which corresponds to the Initial Expenses Loan.   
On the first Payment Date the Fund will have available the amounts under the Liquidity 
Line that will be transferred from the Liquidity Line Sinking Account. 
All payments from the Fund will be transacted through the Treasury Account, following 
instructions from the Sociedad Gestora. 


This prospectus is a translation into English of the original "Folleto Informativo" drafted in Spanish language and registered with the 
"Comisión Nacional del Mercado de Valores" (the Spanish Securities Market Commission, "CNMV") on November 25h, 2005. The "Folleto 
Informativo" drafted in the Spanish language is the only official document, and no document other than the "Folleto Informativo"shall have 
any legal effect or be relied upon with regard to the Note Issue.

The Treasury Account will not be allowed to have a negative balance to the detriment of 
the Fund. The balances in the Treasury Account will remain as available cash  
The amounts deposited into the Collection Account will accrue interest on behalf of the 
Fund, with said interest to be paid monthly (on the first day of each month), calculated 
based on an annual interest rate equal to the rate that results from reducing the Collection 
Account reference rate, which will be the monthly average of the EONIA rates, calculated 
in accordance with the provisions of the Financial Services Contract, by fifteen (15) basis 
points. 
In the event that, at any given moment, the balance in the Collection Account, together 
with the balance of the Treasury Account and the balance of the Liquidity Line Sinking 
Account, were to be greater than or equal to 20% of the Outstanding Nominal Amount of 
the Bonds, the Sociedad Gestora will transfer such excess into the Treasury Surplus 
Account, pursuant to the provisions of section 3.4.4.1. immediately above. 
In the event that the short-term risk rating of the Payment Agent assigned by any of the 
Rating Agencies, which is currently listed as F1+ by Fitch and A-1 by S&P, were 
downgraded to below F1 on the Fitch rating scale and/or below A-1 on the S&P rating 
scale, or if that rating were to be withdrawn, for whatever reason, by any of the Rating 
Agencies, the Sociedad Gestora must initiate the same actions as those established for the 
Collection Account. 
3.4.4.3 
Reinvestment Accounts 
In the event that one of the Sellers were to obtain a rating equal to the highest short term 
rating assigned by both Ratings Agencies, S&P and Fitch, the Sociedad Gestora, after 
informing the CNMV, will proceed to open a bank account on behalf of the Fund at the 
corresponding Seller (the “Rated Seller”), called a “Reinvestment Account”, which will 
be used to receive, on each Collection Date, all of the amounts which the Fund should 
receive from that Seller. The Rated Seller will enter into a contract with the Sociedad 
Gestora, with the latter acting on behalf of and for the account of the Fund, which will 
control the handling of the Reinvestment Account.  
The regulation stipulated in this section must not refer to CREDIFIMO, because, in its 
capacity as a financial credit establishment, it cannot open current accounts. 
In the event that the Seller becomes a Rated Seller, the proportional share of the Reserve 
Fund which has been assigned to it will be added to the Reinvestment Account, from the 
Treasury Account, on the following Payment Date.  
The Rated Seller will provide to the Fund all of the customary services relating to the 
maintenance and administration of said account, in accordance with normal banking 
practices. The Rated Sellers will not charge the Fund any bank charges for the respective 
Reinvestment Accounts. 
The positive balances in favour of the Fund, if any, which occur in the Reinvestment 
Accounts will accrue interest, which will be payable quarterly (on the Business day prior 
to each Payment Date) at a variable rate equal to the Reference Interest Rate EURIBOR. 
With prior instructions from the Sociedad Gestora, on the Business Day prior to each 
Payment Date, the Rated Seller will make the necessary transfers in order to meet the 
obligations of the Fund through the Payment Agent. 
In the event that the rating assigned by either of the Rating Agencies to the short-term risk 
of the Rated Seller is downgraded below F1, according to the rating scale of Fitch and/or

(iii) obtain a guarantee that guarantees that the amounts collected by the Rated Seller as 
the servicer of the Mortgage Loans are deposited into the Reinvestment Account, and that

not exceeding 0.65% of the initial balance of the Securities issue; 
(iv) deposit the revenues of the Participations and the Certificates, every two (2) days, 
into the Reinvestment Account; 
(v) deposit the revenues of the Participations and the Certificates, every day into the 
Reinvestment Account; and 
(vi) find an entity with a short-term rating of F1, on the Fitch rating scale, and A-1+, on 
the S&P rating scale, that is willing to take over, under the same terms and conditions, the 
duties of the Rated Seller in relation to the Reinvestment Account.

must implement the options described in points (i) and (ii) jointly, or else the options 
described in sections (ii) and (vi) jointly. 
If the Rated Seller's rating is F2 on the Fitch scale, the options described in sections (i), 
(iii) and (iii) must be implemented; or else the options described in sections (i) and (iv), or 
the options described in sections (iv), (vi). 
If the Rated Seller's rating is F3 on the Fitch scale, or in the event that such Seller ceases 
to be rated by Fitch, the options described in sections (i), (iii) and (v) must be 
implemented; or else the options described in sections (ii), (iii) and (vi). 
As of the signing of the Articles of Incorporation, none of the Sellers has a rating high 
enough, in accordance with the specifications of this section, to open a Reinvestment 
Account. 
3.4.4.4 
Liquidity Line Sinking Account 
The Fund will have available through the Payment Agent, in accordance with the 
provisions of the Financial Services Contract, a bank account on behalf of the Fund 
(“Liquidity Line Sinking Account”). 
On the Disbursement Date the whole amount of the Liquidity Line will be deposited into 
the Liquidity Line Sinking Account pursuant to the provisions of section 3.4.3.1. of the 
Additional Building Block. 


This prospectus is a translation into English of the original "Folleto Informativo" drafted in Spanish language and registered with the

Informativo" drafted in the Spanish language is the only official document, and no document other than the "Folleto Informativo"shall have

The Fund will transfer to the Liquidity Line Sinking Account, on each Payment Date, and 
in keeping with the Available Funds, the amount determined according to section 3.4.3.1 
of this Additional Building Block. 
The Sociedad Gestora will order transfers from the Liquidity Line Sinking Account to the 
Treasury Account in the following instances and in the amounts indicated as follows: 
(1) The Sociedad Gestora will transfer to the Treasury Account, with good value on the 
Business Day immediately prior to a specified Payment Date, those amounts which, as the 
case may be, are necessary to meet the payment obligations specified in sections (1) to 
(14) of the Payment Priority Order, both inclusive, from funds which are held in the 
Liquidity Line Sinking Account. 
(2) On the Payment Date in which the Outstanding Nominal Balance of the 
Participations and the Certificates falls below 10% of the initial balance of the same and 
the Sociedad Gestora opts for the early termination of the Fund, the entire amount of the 
funds held in the Liquidity Line Sinking Account will be transferred to the Treasury 
Account. 
(3) On the Payment Date on which the Saldo Nominal Pendiente de Cobro of the 
Participations and the Certificates is equal to or less than 6.1% of the initial balance 
thereof, on which date the Liquidity Line will be repaid in full in accordance with the 
provisions of section 3.4.3.1 of the current Additional Building Block, the entire amount 
of the funds held in the Liquidity Line Sinking Account will be transferred to the 
Treasury Account. 
(4) Additionally, on the first Payment Date the maximum amount of the Liquidity Line 
will be transferred to the Treasury Account, and applied according to the provisions of 
section 3.4.3.1. of the Additional Building Block, and the amounts not required to cover 
the shortfall will be repaid on the first Payment Date according to the Payment Priority 
Order, and the full amount of the Liquidity Line may be repaid if there is no shortfall, as 
described in section 3.4.3.1. of this Additional Building Block. 
The balance in the Liquidity Line Sinking Account will be held in available cash. The 
balance in the Liquidity Line Sinking Account, for the account of the Fund, cannot be 
used, in any manner, by the Payment Agent, to offset any kind of amount owed to it by 
the Fund or by related third parties, unless prior written approval from the Sociedad 
Gestora has been obtained. 
The amounts deposited into the Liquidity Line Sinking Account will accrue interest on 
behalf of the Fund, with said interest to be paid monthly (on the last day of each month), 
calculated based on a variable annual interest rate equal to the rate that results from 
reducing the Collection Account reference rate, which will be the monthly average of the 
EONIA rates, calculated in accordance with the provisions of the Financial Services 
Contract, by fifteen (15) basis points, which will be transferred to the Treasury Account 
on the Business Day prior to each Payment Date. 
3.4.5. 
How payments are collected in respect of the assets 
As has been indicated in the Additional Building Block, the payments received from the 
Mortgagors will be deposited into the Collection Account on each Collection Date. The 
Sellers, in accordance with the provisions of section 3.7.1 of the Additional Building 
Block, and acting in their capacity as administrators of the Mortgage Loans assigned to 
the Fund, will not make any payment to the Fund that they have not previously received 
from the Mortgagors.

Allocation to the Liquidity Line Sinking Account pursuant to the provisions

3.4.6.2 
Source and application of funds beginning on the first Payment Date and 
until the last Payment Date or the liquidation of the Fund, exclusive 
On each Payment Date the Sociedad Gestora will proceed in successive order to apply the 
Available Funds in the priority order for payments which is established below for each 
one of them (the “Payment Priority Order”).  
a) 
Available Funds: source and applications. 
1.  
Source: the Available Funds on each Payment Date to meet the payment or 
withholding obligations listed in section 2 infra, will be the amount deposited 
in the Treasury Account which will be comprised of

correspond to the immediately previous three Calculation Periods;  
(b)  the amounts which at any given moment comprise the Reserve Fund, 
transferred, where applicable, to the Reinvestment Account;  
(c)  the earnings produced by the balances in the accounts of the Fund,  
(d)  the Net Amounts received by virtue of the Derivative Contracts,  
(e)  the Technical Advance, if any,  
(f)  on the first Payment Date, the stipulated amount of the Liquidity Line, 
pursuant to the provisions of section 3.4.3.1. of this Additional Building 
Block.

3.4.6.3 
Fund Expenses 
In accordance with the provisions of the Payment Priority Order described in the previous 
section, the Sociedad Gestora will satisfy, and charge to the Fund, all of the Fund 
operating expenses, including both the initial expenses and also the ordinary periodic and 
extraordinary expenses that may accrue throughout its life.  
a) 
Initial Expenses 
The estimate of the initial expenses incurred in the incorporation of the Fund and the 
issue of the Securities is detailed in section 0. of the Securities Note. The initial 
expenses will be paid with part of the proceeds from the Securities and, where 
applicable, the amount drawn down from the Initial Expenses Loan. 
b) 
Expenses throughout the life of the Fund 
The Sociedad Gestora will pay, and charge to the Fund, all of the Fund operating 
expenses, including both the Ordinary Expenses and also the Extraordinary 
Expenses that accrue throughout its life, and such expenses will be paid in their 
respective Payment Priority Order.  
Merely by way of illustration, the Sociedad Gestora will pay the following expenses: 
The following are considered ordinary expenses (“Ordinary Expenses”) 
1. Expenses that may arise from the mandatory administrative verifications, 
registrations and authorisations. 
2. The fees payable to the Ratings Agencies for monitoring and maintaining the 
rating of the Securities. 
3. Expenses relating to the Securities bookkeeping, involving their representation 
by the book-entry system, their admission to trading on the organized secondary 
markets and the maintenance of all of the above. 
4. Fund annual audit expenses. 
5. Bond redemption-related expenses. 
6. Fund and/or Security announcement and notice-related expenses. 
7. Issue Financial Expenses. 
8. The Payment Agent’s fee. 
The following are considered extraordinary expenses (“Extraordinary Expenses”):

3.4.7. 
Other arrangements upon which payments of interest and principal to investors are 
dependent 
3.4.7.1 
Derivative Contracts 
The Sociedad Gestora will enter into, on behalf of and for account of the Fund, three 
Derivative Contracts (one quarterly Derivative Contract, one semi-annual Derivative 
Contract, and one annual Derivative Contract) with BSBP, whose most relevant terms are 
described below. 
The signing of the Derivative Contracts addresses, on one hand, the need to hedge against 
the interest rate risk that exists between the assets (Participations and Certificates) and the 
liabilities (Securities) of the Fund and, on the other hand, the interest rate risk that exists 
as a result of the rate caps and floors stipulated in a percentage of the Mortgage Loans 
pooled in the Fund. 
The parent company of BSBP, TBSCI, will guarantee the obligations of BSBP as 
counterparty to the Derivative Contracts. 
Party A: BSBP. 
Party B: The Sociedad Gestora, on behalf of and for the account of the Fund.  
Settlement Dates:  
The settlement dates will coincide with the Payment Dates, in other words, the 22nd day of 
the months of March, June, September, and December of each year or, if that day is not a 
Business Day, on the next Business Day. The first Payment Day of the Fund will be 22 
March 2006. 
Settlement Periods 
The settlement periods will be the number of days that actually pass between two 
consecutive Settlement Dates, including the first one but excluding the last one. By way 
of exception, the duration of the first contract period will be equivalent to the number of

"Comisión Nacional del Mercado de Valores" (the Spanish Securities Market Commission, "CNMV") on November 25h, 2005. The "Folleto 
Informativo" drafted in the Spanish language is the only official document, and no document other than the "Folleto Informativo"shall have 
any legal effect or be relied upon with regard to the Note Issue.

days that actually pass between the Bond Issue Disbursement Date (inclusive) and 22 
March 2006 (exclusive). 
Annual Derivative Contract 
Amount Payable by Party A on account of the Swap (Annual Derivative Contract) 
The Amount Payable by Party A is the result of multiplying the “Notional Amount of the 
Annual Derivative Contract”, as it is later defined, by the Reference Interest Rate 
established for each Payment Date, as defined in section 4.8 of the Securities Note, 
adjusted by a spread of between –0.06/0%, which must be set by Party A on the Date of 
Incorporation of the Fund and included in the Annual Derivative Contract that is signed 
on that date. In the absence of such notice, the spread will be set at 0%. The Party A 
calculation will be based on the number of days that actually pass with respect to a 360-
day year. At the same time the Sociedad Gestora will also notify the CNMV of this 
additional information to the Prospectus. 
The “Notional Amount of the Annual Derivative Contract” will be the Outstanding 
Nominal Balance of the Non-Defaulted Participations and Certificates that are pooled in 
the Fund and whose interest rate is adjusted annually, on the last day of the Calculation 
Period to the immediately preceding Payment Date. 
Amount Payable by Party B on account of the Swap (Annual Derivative Contract) 
The Amount to be Paid by Party B will be the product, based on the number of days that 
actually pass with respect to a 360-day year, of the “Notional Amount of the Annual 
Derivative Contract”, previously defined, multiplied by the “Swap Calculation Factor”. 
The “Swap Calculation Factor” will be the average 12 month EURIBOR rate for the 
twelve months prior to the beginning of Calculation Period, applying the weightings that 
are indicated in the Annual Derivative Contract.  
Amount Payable by Party A on account of the Cap (Annual Derivative Contract) 
On each Settlement Date, Party A will make a compensatory payment to Party B defined 
in such a way as to mitigate the flows being reduced by the amount that the Party B will 
stop receiving from the Mortgage Loans, that revise their interest rates each year and are 
subject to an Interest Rate Cap, due to the fact of being subject to those interest rate caps. 
The exact methodology used to calculate this amount is defined in the pertinent 
Derivative Contract. 
Amount Payable by Party B on account of the Floor (Annual Derivative Contract) 
On each Settlement Date, Party B will make a compensatory payment to Party A, defined 
in such a way that it is equivalent to the amount that Party A will receive additionally 
from the Mortgage Loans, that revise their interest rates each year and are subject to an 
Interest Rate Floor, due to the fact of being subject to those interest rate floors. The exact 
methodology used to calculate this amount is defined in the pertinent Derivative Contract. 
Semi-Annual Derivative Contract 
Amount Payable by Party A on account of the Swap (Semi-Annual Derivative Contract) 
The Amount Payable by Party A is the result of multiplying the “Notional Amount of the 
Semi-Annual Derivative Contract”, as it is later defined, by the Reference Interest Rate 
established for each Payment Date, as defined in section 4.8 of the Securities Note, 
adjusted by a spread of between +0.02/+0.08%, which must be set by Party A on the Date 
of Incorporation of the Fund and included in the Semi-Annual Derivative Contract that is

the Fund and whose interest rate is adjusted quarterly, on the last day of the Calculation 
Period to the immediately preceding Payment Date. 
Amount Payable by Party B on account of the Swap (Quarterly Derivative Contract) 
The Amount to be Paid by Party B will be the product, based on the number of days that 
actually pass with respect to a 360-day year, of the “Notional Amount of the Quarterly 
Derivative Contract”, previously defined, multiplied by the “Swap Calculation Factor” . 
The “Swap Calculation Factor” will be the average 3 month EURIBOR rate for the 
three months prior to the beginning of Calculation Period, applying the considerations 
that are indicated in the Annual Derivative Contract. 
Amount Payable by Party A on account of the Cap (Quarterly Derivative Contract) 
On each Settlement Date, Party A will make a compensatory payment to Party B defined 
in such a way as to mitigate the flows being reduced by the amount that the Party B will 
stop receiving from the Mortgage Loans, that revise their interest rates each quarter and 
are subject to an Interest Rate Cap, due to the fact of being subject to those interest rate 
caps. The exact methodology used to calculate this amount is defined in the pertinent 
Derivative Contract. 
Amount Payable by Party B on account of the Floor (Quarterly Derivative Contract) 
On each Settlement Date, Party B will make a compensatory payment to Party A, defined 
in such a way that it is equivalent to the amount that Party A will receive additionally 
from the Mortgage Loans, that revise their interest rates quarterly and are subject to an 
Interest Rate Floor, due to the fact of being subject to those interest rate floors. The exact 
methodology used to calculate this amount is defined in the pertinent Derivative Contract. 
In the event of default under the Derivative Contract 
 
Breaches of the Derivative Contracts 
If on the Settlement Date Party B does not pay the amount owed to Party A, the 
corresponding Derivative Contract may be terminated at the request of Party A. In the 
event that a settlement amount is owed, Party A will, if applicable, assume the obligation 
to pay the settlement amount specified under the terms of the corresponding Derivative 
Contract, all in accordance with the Payment Priority Order.  
If on a Payment Date Party A does not meet its payment obligations for the full amount 
that is owed to Party B, the Sociedad Gestora can choose to terminate the corresponding 
Derivative Contract. In this case, (i) Party A will assume the obligation to pay the 
settlement amount specified under the terms of the corresponding Derivative Contract and 
(ii), any amounts payable by Party B to Party A, in accordance with the provisions of the 
corresponding Derivative Contract, will be paid according to the Fund Payment Priority 
Order. 
Notwithstanding the above, except in a situation involving a permanent change in the 
financial equilibrium of the Fund, the Sociedad Gestora, on behalf of and for the account 
of the Fund, will make every effort to always have in place three derivatives contracts 
(one for the Mortgage Loans whose interest rates adjust annually, another for the 
Mortgage Loans whose interest rates adjust semi-annually, and another for the Mortgage 
Loans whose interest rates adjust quarterly).

The settlement amount for each Derivative Contract will be calculated by Party A, as the
